<body class="c19 doc-content">
    <div>
        <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c9 WuvYfpVbPj-c10"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4"></span></p>
    </div>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c9"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c4 WuvYfpVbPj-c22">Posted by Mateusz Jurczyk, Google Project
            Zero</span></p>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8 WuvYfpVbPj-c10"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4"></span></p>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8"><span>When tackling a new vulnerability research target, especially a closed-source one, I
            prioritize gathering as much information about it as possible. This gets especially interesting when
            it&#39;s a subsystem as old and fundamental as the Windows registry. In that case, tidbits of valuable data
            can lurk in forgotten documentation, out-of-print books, and dusty open-source code &ndash; each potentially
            offering a critical piece of the puzzle. Uncovering them takes some effort, but the payoff is often immense.
            Scraps of information can contain hints as to </span><span
            class="WuvYfpVbPj-c2">how</span><span>&nbsp;certain parts of the software are implemented, as well as
        </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c2">why</span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;&ndash; what were
            the design decisions that lead to certain outcomes etc. When seeing the big picture, it becomes much easier
            to reason about the software, understand the intentions of the original developers, and think of the
            possible corner cases. At other times, it simply speeds up the process of reverse engineering and saves the
            time spent on deducing certain parts of the logic, if someone else had already put in the time and
            effort.</span></p>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8 WuvYfpVbPj-c10"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4"></span></p>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8"><span>One great explanation for how to go </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c2">beyond the
            binary</span><span>&nbsp;and utilize all available sources of information was presented by Alex Ionescu in
            the keynote of OffensiveCon 2019 titled </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v%3D2D9ExVc0G10&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260925259&amp;usg=AOvVaw3LnsRqXBHEQsSo_ypMfgN3">&quot;Reversing
                Without Reversing&quot;</a></span><span>. My registry security audit did involve a lot of hands-on
            reverse engineering too, but it was heavily supplemented with information not coming directly from
            ntoskrnl.exe. And while Alex&#39;s talk discussed researching Windows as a whole, this blog post provides a
            concrete case study of how to apply these ideas in practice. The second goal of the post is to consolidate
            all collected materials into a single, comprehensive summary that can be easily accessed by future
            researchers on this topic. The full list may seem overwhelming as it includes some references to overlapping
            information, so the ones I find key have been marked with the &#128273; symbol. I highly recommend reviewing
            these resources, as they provide context that will be helpful for understanding future posts.</span></p>
    <h2 class="WuvYfpVbPj-c15 WuvYfpVbPj-c14" id="h.itt8wv71n0e0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c1">Microsoft Learn</span>
    </h2>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">Official documentation is probably the first and
            most intuitive thing to study when dealing with a new API. For Microsoft, this means the Microsoft Learn
            (formerly MSDN Library), a vast body of technical information maintained for the benefit of Windows software
            developers. It is wholly available online, and includes the following sections and articles devoted to the
            registry:</span></p>

    <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_69lbt69sl425-0 start">

        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0">

            <span>&#128273; </span>

            <span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7">

                <a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/sysinfo/registry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260925792&amp;usg=AOvVaw0agpd0xSGxOkcQNj63yNkS">
                    Registry
                </a>

            </span>

            <span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">
                &nbsp;&ndash; the main page about all registry-related subjects. It contains a wealth of knowledge, and
                is a must read for anyone deeply interested in this system mechanism. It is divided into three sections:
            </span>
        </li>


        <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_69lbt69sl425-1 start">

            <li style="margin-left: 66pt;" class="c8 c24 li-bullet-0">
                <span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7">
                    <a
                        href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/sysinfo/about-the-registry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260926040&amp;usg=AOvVaw2Z-n3Gm2jH6dWyxe8e1FlI">
                        About the Registry
                    </a>

                </span>

                <span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">
                    &nbsp;&ndash; provides an introduction to the registry and many of its fundamental concepts.
                </span>
            </li>
            <li style="margin-left: 66pt;" class="c8 c24 li-bullet-0">
                <span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7">
                    <a
                        href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/sysinfo/using-the-registry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260926310&amp;usg=AOvVaw3x3HEA8m9cEwcqAMxVdroL">
                        Using the Registry
                    </a>
                </span>
                <span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">
                    &nbsp;&ndash; provides several examples of how to perform certain common tasks using the Registry
                    API in
                    C++.</span>
            </li>
            <li style="margin-left: 66pt;" class="c8 c24 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                        href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/sysinfo/registry-reference&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260926535&amp;usg=AOvVaw1ucGm_DnsJrbPjiwB-QnQJ">Registry
                        Reference</a></span><span>&nbsp;&ndash; includes complete documentation of all functions that
                    make
                    up the Registry API (see </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                        href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/sysinfo/registry-functions&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260926667&amp;usg=AOvVaw0M5cMM7jBfGvv6PTHUPgwQ">Registry
                        Functions</a></span><span>), and specifies the </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                        href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/sysinfo/registry-element-size-limits&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260926822&amp;usg=AOvVaw3n9UY5Yu93oMS0YuExsJQG">Registry
                        element size limits</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">.</span></li>
        </ul>

    </ul>


    <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_69lbt69sl425-0">
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/troubleshoot/windows-server/performance/windows-registry-advanced-users&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260927075&amp;usg=AOvVaw3wmHnDsrZ0kapdpVJsrWJr">Windows
                    registry information for advanced users</a></span><span>&nbsp;&ndash; a separate article that
                discusses the principles of the registry. It appears to be somewhat outdated (the latest version
                mentioned is Windows Vista), and based on an old KB256986 article that can be traced back to
            </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://web.archive.org/web/20041014015655/http://support.microsoft.com/kb/256986&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260927250&amp;usg=AOvVaw3gsDKCguqwFzwDZYhnh1v6">at
                    least 2004</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.itprotoday.com/windows-78/inside-windows-nt-registry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260927444&amp;usg=AOvVaw09BQFK_6biwhVlehhEZXEX">Inside
                    the Windows NT Registry</a></span><span>&nbsp;and </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions//cc750583(v%3Dtechnet.10)&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260927582&amp;usg=AOvVaw0ILGQkrYOswH17UJx985Ye">Inside
                    the Registry</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;&ndash; two articles
                published by Mark Russinovich in the Windows NT Magazine in 1997 and 1999, respectively.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/it-pro/windows-2000-server/cc974061(v%3Dmsdn.10)&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260927802&amp;usg=AOvVaw3alclpBc43QVp2dWGV-VkV">Windows
                    2000 Registry Reference</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;&ndash; a web
                mirror of regentry.chm, an official help file bundled with the Windows 2000 Resource Kit. It includes a
                brief introduction to the registry followed by detailed descriptions of the standard registry content,
                i.e. keys and values used for advanced configuration of the system and applications.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_69lbt69sl425-1 start">
        <li style="margin-left: 66pt;" class="c8 c24 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/previous-versions/windows/it-pro/windows-server-2003/cc778196(v%3Dws.10)&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260928024&amp;usg=AOvVaw1arlS6ioKQqunhQ-EuKL3Z">Windows
                    Server 2003 Resource Kit Registry Reference</a></span><span
                class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;&ndash; a similar, but more recent reference for Windows
                Server 2003.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_69lbt69sl425-0">
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/perfctrs/using-the-registry-functions-to-consume-counter-data&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260928279&amp;usg=AOvVaw0edjiiNj9ftcHQWWnkGex6">Using
                    the Registry Functions to Consume Counter Data</a></span><span
                class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;&ndash; information about collecting performance data through
                the registry pseudo-keys: HKEY_PERFORMANCE_DATA, HKEY_PERFORMANCE_TEXT and
                HKEY_PERFORMANCE_NLSTEXT.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/win32/devnotes/offline-registry-library-portal&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260928498&amp;usg=AOvVaw0RKTlr3-wRaNznkQcKeuof">Offline
                    Registry Library</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;&ndash; complete
                documentation of the built-in Windows offreg.dll library, which can be used to inspect / operate on
                registry hives without loading them in the operating system.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span>Registry system call documentation, e.g.
            </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/ddi/wdm/nf-wdm-zwcreatekey&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260928745&amp;usg=AOvVaw0b8--9rg8cL3tmxL0qaruP">ZwCreateKey</a></span><span
                class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;&ndash; a reference guide to the kernel-mode support of the
                registry, which reveals numerous details about how it works internally and how the high-level API
                functions are implemented under the hood.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/kernel/filtering-registry-calls&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260928982&amp;usg=AOvVaw22v1Rw2J7WBijPJdxhruLN">Filtering
                    Registry Calls</a></span><span>&nbsp;&ndash; a set of eight articles detailing how to correctly
                implement </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c2">registry callbacks</span><span
                class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;as a kernel driver developer.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_69lbt69sl425-1 start">
        <li style="margin-left: 66pt;" class="c8 c24 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/ddi/wdm/nf-wdm-cmregistercallbackex&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260929252&amp;usg=AOvVaw1Mlmkd6d_H9p7deMfmC9c1">CmRegisterCallbackEx
                    function (wdm.h)</a></span><span>&nbsp;&ndash; documentation of the CmRegisterCallbackEx routine
                used for registering callbacks. From there, one can browse to other relevant pages, such as the
                documentation of the </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/ddi/wdm/nc-wdm-ex_callback_function&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260929403&amp;usg=AOvVaw10Rr8gExyjf8OxneIb9MZw">callback
                    function prototype</a></span><span>, and further to the documentation of all of the
                operation-specific structures (such as </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/ddi/wdm/ns-wdm-_reg_create_key_information&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260929551&amp;usg=AOvVaw1oDgmvtzyO_z0YnuKUVCfZ">REG_CREATE_KEY_INFORMATION</a></span><span
                class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">).</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_69lbt69sl425-0">
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-rrp/0fa3191d-bb79-490a-81bd-54c2601b7a78&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260929778&amp;usg=AOvVaw2VamwJMFBN_uq1JE1TXYyk">[MS-RRP]:
                    Windows Remote Registry Protocol</a></span><span>&nbsp;&ndash; technical specification of the RPC
                protocol used by the Remote Registry feature.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <h2 class="WuvYfpVbPj-c15 WuvYfpVbPj-c14" id="h.36a9b3uw2m8z"><span></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c1">Blogs and
            online resources</span></h2>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">Due to the fact that the registry stores a
            substantial amount of traces of user activity, it is a popular source of information in forensic
            investigations. As a result, a number of articles and blog posts have been published throughout the years,
            focusing on the internal hive structure, registry-related kernel objects, and recovering deleted data. Below
            is the list of non-official registry resources I have managed to find online, from earliest to
            latest:</span></p>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8 WuvYfpVbPj-c10"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4"></span></p>
    <ul style="padding: 0;" class="lst-kix_80vdbxrca7qi-0 start">
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=http://pogostick.net/~pnh/ntpasswd/WinReg.txt&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260930285&amp;usg=AOvVaw1lQoK1mdLSLZKgZ54JV54j">WinReg.txt</a></span><span>,
                author unknown (signed as B.D.) &ndash; documentation of the hive binary formats in Windows 3.x
                (</span><span>SHCC3.10</span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">), Windows 95 (CREG) and Windows
                NT (regf) based on reverse engineering. It was likely the first public write-up outlining the
                undocumented structure of the hives.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://web.archive.org/web/20190717124313/http://www.beginningtoseethelight.org/ntsecurity/index.htm&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260930566&amp;usg=AOvVaw0bzp_31FNjPoRkIucdMJJ5">Security
                    Accounts Manager</a></span><span>, author unknown (signed as
            </span><span>clark@hushmail.com</span><span>) &ndash; a comprehensive article primarily focused on the user
                management internals in Windows 2000 and XP, dissecting a number of binary structures used by the
            </span><span>SAM</span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;component. Since user and credential
                management is highly tied to the registry (all of the authentication data is stored there), the article
                also includes a &quot;Registry Structure&quot; section that explains the encoding of regf hive
                files.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span>&#128273; </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/msuhanov/regf/blob/master/Windows%2520registry%2520file%2520format%2520specification.md&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260930969&amp;usg=AOvVaw01AppKMx17kxmQ40zJDio0">Windows
                    registry file format specification</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">, Maxim
                Suhanov &ndash; a high-quality and relatively up-to-date specification of the regf format versions 1.3
                to 1.6, with extra bits of information regarding the ancient versions 1.1 and 1.2.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/libyal/libregf/blob/main/documentation/Windows%2520NT%2520Registry%2520File%2520(REGF)%2520format.asciidoc&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260931245&amp;usg=AOvVaw3TQI8ty6cYDNqKABWKkhBp">Windows
                    NT Registry File (REGF) format specification</a></span><span>, Joachim Metz &ndash; another
                independently developed specification of the regf format associated with the
            </span><span>libregf</span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;library.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://moyix.blogspot.com/search/label/registry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260931479&amp;usg=AOvVaw2jWtpJubQ_9AD1holuohYV">Push
                    the Red Button</a></span><span>, Brendan Dolan-Gavitt (</span><span>moyix</span><span
                class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">) &ndash; a personal blog focused on security, reverse engineering
                and forensics. It contains a number of interesting registry-related posts dating back to
                2007-2009.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://windowsir.blogspot.com/search/label/Registry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260931760&amp;usg=AOvVaw2KjYL-Dj6josNqSkm2x6p9">Windows
                    Incident Response</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">, Harlan Carvey &ndash; a
                technical blog dedicated to incident response and digital analysis of Windows, with a variety of posts
                dealing with the registry published between 2006-2022.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://dfir.ru/?s%3Dregistry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260932015&amp;usg=AOvVaw3XVMCaxW7BAeqkb3-j8Jaw">My
                    DFIR Blog</a></span><span>, Maxim Suhanov &ndash; another blog concentrating on digital forensics
                with many mentions of the Windows registry. It provides some original information that&#39;s hard to
                find elsewhere, see e.g. </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://dfir.ru/2020/08/15/containerized-registry-hives-in-windows/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260932256&amp;usg=AOvVaw3P5QUsQogwenB2aMUZPo46">Containerized
                    registry hives in Windows</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.mandiant.com/resources/blog/digging-up-the-past-windows-registry-forensics-revisited&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260932565&amp;usg=AOvVaw15OqdOqe4rurf0H8R9AqXE">Digging
                    Up the Past: Windows Registry Forensics Revisited</a></span><span
                class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">, David Via &ndash; a blog post by Mandiant discussing the recovery
                of data from registry hives and transactional logs.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://scorpiosoftware.net/2020/07/17/creating-registry-links/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260932855&amp;usg=AOvVaw0FpH1t8d08TSokmWL0tNok">Creating
                    Registry Links</a></span><span>&nbsp;and </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://scorpiosoftware.net/2022/04/15/mysteries-of-the-registry/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260933035&amp;usg=AOvVaw1Qn3SYF03C4J05-L-DQ5CM">Mysteries
                    of the Registry</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">, Pavel Yosifovich &ndash; two
                blog posts covering the creation of symbolic links in the registry, and its overall internal
                structure.</span></li>
        <li style="margin-left: 46pt;" class="c13 c14 li-bullet-0"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                    href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_Registry&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260933296&amp;usg=AOvVaw1jNF0kLz5Ia_x2u7yAbSWI">Windows
                    Registry</a></span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">, Wikipedia contributors &ndash; as
                usual, Wikipedia doesn&#39;t disappoint, and even though the article includes few deeply technical
                details, it features extensive sections on the history of the registry, its high level design and role
                in the system.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8 WuvYfpVbPj-c10"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4"></span></p>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8"><span>Furthermore</span><span>, </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c7"><a
                href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://devblogs.microsoft.com/oldnewthing/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1719419260933753&amp;usg=AOvVaw0EWx8a08YtEQfY3wWCBWAY">The
                Old New Thing</a></span><span>&nbsp;is a fantastic, technical blog exploring the quirks, design
            decisions, and historical context behind Windows features. It is written by a Microsoft employee of over 30
            years, Raymond Chen, with an astounding consistency of one post per day. While the blog posts are not
        </span><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c2">technically</span><span
            class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4">&nbsp;documentation, they are very highly regarded in the community and
            can be considered a de-facto Microsoft knowledge resource &ndash; only more fun than Microsoft Learn. Over
            the course of the last 20+ years, Raymond would sometimes write about the registry, sharing interesting
            behind-the-scenes stories and anecdotes concerning this feature. I have tried to find and compile all of the
            relevant registry-related posts in the single list below:</span></p>
    <p class="WuvYfpVbPj-c8 WuvYfpVbPj-c10"><span class="WuvYfpVbPj-c5 WuvYfpVbPj-c4"></span></p>
